Therefore, given that Akt phoshorylates and inactivates GSK3β [19], we hypothesised that Akt-dependent inactivation of GSK3β might be responsible for Notch potentiation. To address this question, we looked at the N1-IC-induced Notch response in primary human CD4+ T-cells treated with the GSK3β inhibitor lithium chloride. Increasing concentrations of LiCl induced a dramatic increase in Notch signalling (Fig. 3A).">

Pruning agenda with beam width 50</debug><ekb complete="true" id="TEXT00002_IO-49000" timestamp="20190628T133652"><input type="text"><paragraphs><paragraph file="/Users/wbeaumont/drum/etc/Data/WP/TEXT00002_IO-49000" id="paragraph1">Previous data has suggested that inactivation of GSK3β by the Wingless pathway enhanced Notch signals by preventing inhibitory phosphorylation of N-IC by GSK3β [18]. Therefore, given that Akt phoshorylates and inactivates GSK3β [19], we hypothesised that Akt-dependent inactivation of GSK3β might be responsible for Notch potentiation. To address this question, we looked at the N1-IC-induced Notch response in primary human CD4+ T-cells treated with the GSK3β inhibitor lithium chloride. Increasing concentrations of LiCl induced a dramatic increase in Notch signalling (Fig. 3A).
